## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental problem in chemical kinetics. The rate law typically depends on powers of concentration, but time-dependence may arise from substitution of other species' integrated rate laws or external forcing.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, first-order reaction)
- Second-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of same species)
- nth-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reactions)
- Mixed order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics / saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis)
- Second-order with second species substituted: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (pseudo-rate law after integrating another species)
- Time-dependent forcing with decay: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * t (linear time-dependent source/sink)
- Consecutive reaction (substituted): dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * A (intermediate in consecutive reactions)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (substrate inhibition)
- Fractional order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 (fractional order with constant production)
- Cooperative kinetics (Hill-type): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding/reaction)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative proportionality to concentration (dA/dt = -k*A) indicates first-order consumption/decay with exponential solution
- Rate proportional to A*(constant - A) suggests autocatalytic or logistic growth where a reactant is also a catalyst
- Rational functions of A (e.g., A/(K+A)) indicate enzyme-mediated or surface-catalyzed reactions with saturation
- Explicit time dependence in rate law often arises from elimination of intermediate species concentrations via their analytical solutions
- Rate proportional to A^n with non-integer n suggests complex reaction mechanisms or effective/lumped kinetics
- Sign of dA/dt changing at specific A values indicates equilibrium points or steady states in reversible reactions
- Product of exponential in t and power of A suggests coupled differential equations where one species was solved analytically
- Polynomial in A (quadratic or cubic) can represent multiple competing reaction pathways with different molecularities
- Rate laws independent of A but dependent on t suggest zero-order kinetics with time-varying external conditions (e.g., photolysis with varying light)
